<Text>Had no idea this cozy little theater was so close to home! It's on the small side - both stage and seating - but the seats are comfortable and there's no need for microphones. Acoustics are great and there are no bad seats. Thoroughly enjoyed myself here. The company puts on 5 or 6 shows a year, with matinees on Saturdays. < user_id>
105032707722372186574< /user_id>
<name>Adam Zale</name><time>1445714798233</time><Rate>4< /Rate>< Review>
Cafe Cabaret is an awesome cafe. There is some hit and miss stuff that keeps me from dropping down the 5th star but it's definitely a good cafe to keep on your to-go-to list. Atmosphere is cute inside and there is patio seating facing the side street with a little fountain. It gets very warm inside during the summer.

What really makes them special is the sheer effort you see them put into the menu and the venue. They clearly care about making it work and even though service has been spotty from time to time, it being family run makes that seem okay. The menu is vast and they have specialty foods which I can get nowhere else. From the lebanese menu, the traditional breakfast menu, occasional buffets ... man they have gyros! No one else around here has gyros. And CREPES! You can get delicious sweet or savory crepes for breakfast!

That said the coffee is super hit and miss. The mochas are powder and a little off target compared to the starbucks formulas. Smoothies are decent enough but nothing to die for. I've had some blended drinks and they're tasty enough.

Four stars for a business that really makes an effort.< /Review>

< review>
Cheap & Easy.

Not just the title to my forthcoming autobiography, but a description of Little Caesars.

I know it's not the greatest.

I know it's not "artisanal" pizza made by paisanos, newly arrived from Italy.

But hey, it's cheap, fast & easy!  Remind you of anyone you know? ;P

When having a gathering and in a bind on what to feed the horde of hungry orcs, just say "Hail Caesar!".  $5 gets you a large cheese or pepperoni, innocently waiting for you to take them home.  No utensils needed.  Just grab a slice, sprinkle some chili peppers and/or parmesan cheese if that's what you fancy and enjoy the cheesy, unctuous goodness of cheap & filling pizza.

Everytime I've dropped by at this location, it's been hassle-free all the way.  Parking can be a little tight, but nothing major.

Sometimes I'll have the deep dish pizza, crazy bread and/or the wings, mostly because others want them, but I stick to a large pepperoni.  I'm not a fan of pineapple on pizza, but they do you have Hawaiian pizza for those that are.

I was good today!  Only had 4 slices.......:P

Recommend!

NOMNOMNOMNOMNOMNOMNOM<//review>

<text>I made dinner reservations for my wife and I to celebrate 15 years of marriage. The Smoking Goat provided a great vibe from the moment we turned direction to enter from the sidewalk. We were noticed and approached by the host with great energy, offered congratulations for our anniversary, and promptly seated. Our server was made aware of our celebration and maintained a super-friendly vibe all night never seeming rushed or distracted despite the many tables he looked to be taking care of. Each appetizer, entree, and dessert item was wonderfully balanced with a great care and developed flavor. Although my wife and I typically lean to what many would consider more ‚Äúexotic‚Äù tastes, we will definitely go back to The Smoking Goat for tried and true classic techniques that produce amazing food. Again, compliments to the staff for maintaining a respectful, professional, friendly, and comfortable vibe without ever seeming stuffy or uptight.< /text><Pictures>None<//Pictures><response>None<//response>< gmapID>

</record></dataset><record>
<userid>103242576492476179802</userid><Name>Ryan Fong<//Name><time>1618439582989< /time>< Rate>
5</Rate>
< text>
Tried The Smoking Goat for San Diego Restaurant week dinner $50 per person and was blown away! The food was presented beautifully and prepared to perfection. Started off with the Duck Liver Pate for first course, Duroc Pork Chop for main entree, and Strawberry Short Cake for dessert. Added some Hand-Cut Duckfat Truffle Fries and a bottle of Bordeaux Blank Smoking Goat Wine on the side. Are you drooling yet? I was for sure. Highly recommend this place for restaurant week. The food was tasty, but we were duped into believing we could dine in the restaurant or on the patio with full service. I had to give a credit card number to secure our ‚Äúreservation‚Äù - for eating out of takeout containers on the sidewalk.Nothing was accurately updated on their website or for Open Table. When we arrived we were told our patio reservation was ready, that we would have to order at the podium and to-go boxes would be dropped off. The patio was uninviting, and there was no cocktail service. When we placed our order we were told 2 of the 5 options for entrees were unavailable. This happened to the next group of diners who tried to order. Why not just say what you are out of when you hand the menus over? We took our to-go food back to the house, and set the table and had a nice dinner, but would never normally pay $200 for a takeout dinner. I understand these are hard times for restaurants and their employees. I left a $10 tip for the guy who put in our order, but I felt like we were duped into showing up for a dining experience that they never intended on delivering. If you are looking for decent takeout at a premium price, go for it. I will never eat here again, not because the food was bad, but because of the deceptive approach during these trying times.</Review>

As good as it gets for Classic French Cuisine. We made the drive all the way down from Carlsbad and are planning on doing it again.

<Date>1578889234873<//Date>< Text>
Lovely French restaurant
I love French food and there aren't that many French restaurants in San Diego. The Smoking Goat had been on my radar for quite awhile and I finally had dinner there. The restaurant itself is charming with a European vibe. I had the pear salad which was outstanding with its mix of ingredients , and the 1/2 Gone Straw Farms Chicken. The latter is served in a skillet with mashed potatoes and a vegetable medley. A nice sauce gives it added flavor.
Yes, they have salmon and scallops. There's a lamb dish also with pasta that sounded yummy (and for which I'd make an exception in terms of red meat) but it sounded more Italian than French.
They change the menu four times a year (seasonally) so I'll look forward to seeing their other menus. I'd definitely go back.< /Text>

We went for restaurant week and they were clearly overwhelmed.   The service was very slow and much of what came out was over salted.  It took 30 minutes for the appitizers to come to the table the 45 more minutes for the entrees and another 30 minutes for the desserts.  We ordered a few of the escargot appetizers which were very nicely prepared, however,  the octopus appetizers were way overcooked and the French onion soup was very salty.  All the entrees were way too salty and the medium rare stakes were burnt black on the outside, though medium rare on the inside, the pork chop and salmon were cooked much more appropriately.  Finally the deserts, the goat cheese cheesecake was perfect, and the flourless chocolate cake was very good, however,  the panna cotta looked and tasted like a jello pudding gone very wrong. <userid>107946650428202074673</userid>< name>
Jason Goldwater< /name>
<Time>1597971833769< /Time>< Rating>
5</Rating>
< text>
Rarely post reviews but had a truly standout experience at The Smoking Goat, during COVID no less. I'm a relatively recent transplant to San Diego and while I've dined at some decent restaurants, there hasn't been a place that has offered a truly standout experience like I had last night.

While we of course regret not being able to enjoy the restaurant indoors, the outdoor dining was quite pleasant. We were waited on by Pascal, a young and charming waiter who, it turns out, had only been working there for a couple months. I was actually quite surprised when I learned this, as he knew the menu inside and out and made several great recommendations. His service was attentive but unobtrusive, and he seemed to really enjoy his job. Despite seeming somewhat timid--greater confidence will come with more experience, and he has every reason to be confident--Pascal was a great waiter. We also had the pleasure of meeting Alex, the manager, a lovely gentlemen who cares deeply about his restaurant and his clients. He very nicely checked on us several times throughout the evening and engaged us in welcome conversation.

I went with a couple friends and we ordered appetizers (or entrees as they're called in France), consisting of the Heirloom Tomato Salad, the Duck Liver Pate, and the Baked Brie, along with the Duckfat Truffle Fries. All were truly excellent, and the toasted sliced baguette that accompanied each dish was delicious and exactly the right mix of soft and crunchy. My personal favorite was the Brie. This is because I grew up in France and have an appreciation for cheese, but especially so as the Brie was nicely aged, bringing out the unique smells and tastes (rather than the tasteless straight-out-of-the-fridge bland cheeses that restaurants usually serve).

We also enjoyed several drinks, including the Mule, a glass of wine and a Kronenbourg 1664 Blanc. I'd say the low point of the meal was the Mule, which while adequate wasn't very impressive--but this is truly a testament to how great the rest of the meal, drinks and service were.

After our "entrees," we enjoyed the Morbier, accompanied by several desert wines and cocktails including a Kir Royale, a lovely glass of Port, and something Alex recommended that I wasn't familiar with: a glass of 2009 Chateau Dauphine Loupiac. The Morbier, like the Brie earlier, was excellent and, like all our other dishes, very nicely plated with accoutrements including fruit, jam, baguette, nuts, and so on. The standout drink for me was the Loupiac, which I *highly* recommend if you like nice desert wines, although one of my friends preferred the port and the other preferred the Kir Royale. Hard to go wrong!

To wrap things up, we shared a slice of phenomenal goat cheese cheesecake.

We hadn't intended on having such a large meal, but the experience was so awesome that we simply couldn't pull ourselves away from the table. I'm already trying to mentally calendar my next visit!</text>

< text>
This is your next culinary adventure! The smoking goat serves well thought out menus that includes the freshest and most sustainable ingredients in the most visually delicious way. Our first course was the pate plate that had a surprisingly clean finish for most pates have a strong organ after taste this dish was instead smooth as butter. We paired this and second with a smoking goat Rose but switch to a pinot for the final course.
Or next course was a bright and abundant nicoise salad with a well balanced dressing that let all the flavors stand on their own. The final course was a gorgeous 2 " thick piece  of salmon that as Alex, the manager explained it was swimming yesterday . It was served on my favorite pasta, an Israeli couscous. The Smoking Goat is located in a North Park bedroom community with a great vibe. I drive down from Encinitas to enjoy a great meal in a easy going environment that feels like home. Enjoy your next culinary adventure here!!</text>

< Text>
Dark and cozy I'd imagine this would be an amazing restaurant for a date.  It has been on my list to try for some time so my friends and I decided to make this our Restaurant Week outing.   I started with the duck fat fries which were amazing!  Seriously some of the best fries I've ever had.  My second course was duck breast.  It was tender and very flavorful and the butternut squash puree was just the right side.  I sampled my sisters pork belly with polenta and was blown away.  Delicious.  Of the desserts the cheesecake was the best.
The food was definitely 5 stars.  It could be because of restaurant week volume but the service was extremely slow.  We were there almost 2 hours and not because we were lingering over courses.  Perhaps on a normal evening the service would have been more prompt.  I will be more than happy to come back and see!< /Text>

<UserId.>105929644731397610584<//UserId.><username>Douglas LeClair<//username><Date>1400006555605<//Date><rating>4<//rating><review>Was looking forward to trying The Smoking Goat from a friend's recommendation and it didn't disappoint!

My wife and I dined here last evening and it was a hot evening so we asked to be seated at a patio table. The decor was rustic.  The menu on their web site seems to not have been posted for 3 or 4 months so we didn't know what to expect on availability or entree prices.

I can see the patio being obnoxious for people expecting a quiet romantic meal out as it is right next to a really busy bar patio where intoxicated patrons are being raucous and smoking. Not really the fault of the restaurant but a good thing to know and be aware of -- it didn't bother us and provided some good people watching.

We started the meal off with the Duck Fat Truffle Fries. Easily exceeds the truffle fries at Bertrand at Mr. A's. Bordering on almost too salty, the herbs and spices and the mustard seed aioli countered some of it. Very rich but also very addicting! The portions were very generous considering the quality.

My wife ordered the butternut squash ravioli which came with pancetta, and deep fried brussel sprouts. Very good, you can tell the effort put into the dish and everything was house made.

I ordered the Beef Short Ribs and it was nothing short of decadent. The ribs were completely fork tender and fell apart and melted in your mouth. Lots of good flavors going on throughout the meal. Their greens are amazing as well as the sweet mashed yams.

We definitely want to come back next time to check out the desserts!<//review>< pics>

< userid>
101520184619030112062<//userid>
<username>Tricia Pooladi</username>< Review>
For a friend's birthday we came here for the first time and ate everything family style.  The elegant farmhouse cuisine was delicate and hearty at the same time.

Appetizers
Fried Octopus - a single, fresh, tender arm (one person could have eaten it alone) perfectly fried with a thin, perfectly even coating of crisp batter.
***** Raclette Au Gratin - delicious cheesy fingerling potatoes - cooked perfectly.
***** Jidori Chicken Liver Pate - although this is on the menu as a side we got it as an appetizer.  I love pate, and they make a good one, so if you like pate, definitely give it a try.

Entrees
**** Australian Spring Lamb Loin - Lamb is usually my favorite, and in this case it was everyone else's favorite, but not mine.  It was seasoned perfectly, and the accompanying vegetables were perfect - the lamb was just a tad tougher than I feel it should have been, although the flavor was perfect.  Admitted, I am typically the pickiest about this particular meat.
***** Pan Roasted Alaskan Halibut - Delicious, fresh, and for some reason, the roasted cauliflower on this dish was one of the best components of any of the food we tried.  I mean we seriously contemplated asking if we could order it as a stand-alone-side.
***** Handmade Ricotta and English Pea Ravioli - The raviolis were large and tenderly handmade, with just the right amount of sauce.
**** Duck Leg Confit - The duck was cooked perfectly and well-paired

Dessert
**** Creme Brulee - I use creme brulee as my standardized dessert.  The consistency was perfect and a perfect layer of crispy burnt sugar on top.
***** Griddled Banana Bread - I love bananas, I love banana bread, yum, yum, yum.
***** Goat Cheese Cheesecake - if you have never had goat cheese cheesecake, this is an excellent one to have as your first.  It was perfectly balanced (sometimes the goat cheese can be too pungent or the consistency can be off with this type of cheesecake).  I mean seriously, it was perfect.

* denotes dish rating<//Review>

<UserId.>108260930365846169531< /UserId.><resp>None< /resp><pics>None<//pics>< text>
I've been here a number of times over the years and never had a single complaint up until the most recent dinner. We had made reservations for dinner and my woman has been craving for Smoking Goat for a while now.

I nearly forgot it was restaurant week and didn't plan on having their prix fixe meal offered on a regular basis either. When we got seated, I asked for the regular menu as I didn't have a huge appetite for 3 courses. The server replied rudely and said it was "all or nothing" as they apparently weren't serving anything else but just the SDRW menu.

This is understandable as I know they want to make the kitchen more focused on just those items and I would have been okay with that if I was well aware ahead of time. This level of rudeness doesn't fly with me and are the type of things that get me heated. I ended up calling the server out and mentioned how disrespectful that was and asked to speak with a manager.

The manager finally came by and apologized. He accommodated us and allowed us to do just entrees. It was their fault for not contacting us and he was aware of that. We would have had the better bang for our buck with the 3-course meal anyway but all I wanted was an entree and not having to stuff myself. But the main reason I asked him to come over was to rectify the disrespectful service.

He asked if we wanted a new server and I really didn't care too much if the same person continued serving us. But let me tell you, not once did the server apologize to us in any manner throughout the course of the night.

I won't go around mentioning the name of the server like other disgruntled reviewers do in similar situations so I'll leave it at that. What I do hope is that this person learns and uses the right level of respect, especially when you're working in the service industry. Sure, most patrons would put up with this type of crap but there are others like myself who won't think twice to speak out.

It appears that the most recent substandard reviewers have had similar experiences with their server. Let's hope they can work on their service again and bring it up to par as before.< /text>
